text:
Easy & so good!  I didn't have any winter squash, but I added baby carrots & 
sliced zucchini.  One thing I did different, I put the root vegetables (onion, 
potatoes & carrots) in one bowl & the more delicate vegetables (peppers &
zucchini) in another bowl, they I divided the oil/vinegar/herb mixture between
the two bowls.  I put the root vegetables in the oven first & let them roast for 30
minutes before adding the other vegetables at the last 10 or 15 minutes.  That
way they stayed bright colored & didn't get mushy.  I took them to a potluck dinner
& there wasn't a single bite leftover.  Great, healthy recipe!

Just so everyone knows, the only way to make this recipe and have it turn out well is to use FRESH ROSEMARY AND THYME! I made the mistake thinking that it wouldn't be a big deal using dried...but I was wrong.  I've read so many good things about this recipe to only have it turn out pretty bad.  The dried thyme overpowered the taste of the dish. I may make this again (using fresh spices) but I still have a bad taste in my mouth from the veggies I just made. Either way, it was a learning experience!

text:
This recipe was SO good! I really had never found a good way to roast vegetables that didn't sound complicated (put this veggie in, take this one out, lower the temp, put the oven on broil, stir every 3 minutes...), until now! I took this dish to my brother's house, and they wanted to keep all the leftovers! The only thing I did differently was to omit butternut squash, and up the ratio of balsamic vinegar to olive oil. Oh, I also used salt and pepper in the dressing. I used 1 large red onion, 1 sweet potato, 3 new potatoes, half a bag of baby carrots, grape tomatoes, crimini mushrooms, red bell peppers, zucchini, and I used dried rosemary, thyme and basil (I already had dried) for the seasonings. I did the root vegetables on one foil-lined baking pan, and the more delicate veggies on another pan. I found mine burned after about 15 minutes at 475, so I lowered the temp. to 450 and just cooked longer. With the addition of the time in the oven at 475, the root vegetables took about 45-50 minutes, and the other veggies took about 25-30, stirring both. 
This recipe tasted SO good, though, and I have gotten requests to make it for holidays and other family gatherings. Thanks for sharing it!

text:
FANTASTIC!  What a wonderful way to bring out the vibrant colors, and flavor of vegetables; such a versatile recipe.  I forwent the sweet potatoes and squash, and don't care for rosemary so omitted those.  Used red potatoes w/skins instead of yukons, and added some fresh broccoli.  The broccoli was to die for roasted!  I kept all measurements the same except had to add a bit more EVOO.  I added some garlic powder(was afraid to add garlic cloves for fear of burning and becoming bitter) and added 1 tsp. basil, 1 tsp. dried crushed thyme.  (didn't have fresh) Fresh cracked pepper and salt at the end.  This is just perfect.  Did it in big roaster pan and just loosely covered w/foil and turned every 10 minutes as stated for the 35 and they still browned while I think that bit of foil just loosely laid overtop helped them 'steam' a bit and no veggie was too crunchy or mushy.  Served w/oven-broiled lamb and baguettes and it was a complete meal.

text:
If you are looking for the quickest, easiest, best tasting recipe of roasted vegetables, look no further! I've been trying to find a good recipe for a long time, and tried many variations, but this is the absolute best.  I made it in a 450F preheated oven for about 45 mins with gold potatoes, squash, yellow onion, red bell pepper, and carrots, using dry rosemary, thyme, basil, just a pinch of garlic powder and red pepper, salt+pepper,  and balsamic vinegar and corn oil (was out of olive).   Some tips: Balsamic vinegar (not lemon), red bell pepper, and basil are a must for me in this recipe, all the other ingredients can be added or subtracted depending on what you have on hand. If using dry herbs, use about 1/4 of what the recipe calls for (proportions in the recipe are for fresh herbs). When making the seasoning mixture, you will know the right amount of salt when the mixture tastes a little salty and the sour taste goes away a bit. Use a large shallow pan, loosely cover with foil, and gentry stir the veggies every 10 mins.   I did not separate the veggies into different bowls, and did add the squash. I diced the squash into large peaces, and it turned out perfectly! It was not mushy at all, but completely cooked through.  The dish turned out beautiful, good enough for a weeknight dinner or to entertain guests. All the veggies were evenly browned, very moist (but not greasy), and aromatic. I surved the veggies with roasted chicken, and there were no leftovers.

text:
Delicious!  Love the addition of balsamic vinegar.  I usually just do oil and rosemary but the balsamic really kicked the flavor up a notch.  **On a side note, I highly recommend either dropping the temp significantly or using a different oil.  Olive oil has a very low smoke point of 325.  When oil smokes, it releases carcinogens into the air and free radicals within the oil. Not good!  I cooked mine at 425 with canola oil which has a higher smoke point. Just something to keep in mind if you are concerned about these kinds of things.

Delicious! I made this to go with a roasted chicken seasoned with "essence of emmeril"! I added carrots quartered lengthwise, and drizzled the drippings from the roasted chicken over the top before cooking. 
Due to my cutting everything into long wedges, it took about 50 minutes. 
I suppose those with a southern taste for their veggies might  like them cooked quite a bit longer till soft. 
Note: As a general culinary school rule, fresh to dry is usually 3 to 1, one tablespoon fresh equals one teaspoon dry, and if the dried has been sitting around awhile, you might want to add a bit extra. Give the dried herbs time to absorb some of the liquids before the cooking process for best results...

text:
Yummy. And so good for you. I can snack on veggies, this recipe makes it so easy to. Fresh herbs make a world of difference. It takes a little more effort to get the leaves off the stem, but it will make or break this recipe. The OIL needs to be DRASTICALLY REDUCED. Not even to half the 1/4 c but a couple tablespoons to lightly coat. I used about half of what the recipe called for, as I thought the 475 degree temp called to bake the veggies would require it to keep from burning, but as I was pouring the 1/4c it still seemed an outrageous amount of oil. So I amended to half of what the recipe called for and it was still too much for me, in my opinion. Unless I'm frying I use oil in tsp/tbsp measurements. My only other suggestion is stick to robust vegetables, that can handle that high of a temperature. I would omit the bell pepper or add in the last 10-15 minutes. I used sweet potato and squash, carrots, pearl onions, a Vidalia onion (which I'll omit next time - did not hold up in the heat) and cauliflower which turned out beautifully at the suggested bake time. As well as asparagus and bell pepper, mushrooms, which I'll add in the last 10-15 minutes the next time. But this is a very yummy staple.

text:
This is a fantastic addition to any meal. The first time I tried this recipe, it took quite a while to bake because the squash takes longer to bake through, so everything else mildly suffered by being a bit over-cooked and vary dark (but still tasty!) The second time around, we had friends coming over, on of them being a very good cook, so I was really trying to impress them. I changed the recipe a bit thoug. I used more EVOO so that the pieces could be coated more and replaced some of the ingredients. I took out the squash and instead added brussel sprouts, left some of the onion separated with more layers and whole garlic cloves (still wrapped in it's skin). I also lowered the temparature of the oven to avoid burning of the onion and covered it with foil for the first 20 minutes or so. It turned out DELICIOUS. Everyone loved it, and garlic becomes a whole different beast when eaten whole once it's been baked~ just melts in your mouth! I will definitely be making more of this to add some sort of healthiness to any of our meals.

This dish was great.  I cooked it ahead of my dinner party as I was concerned about trying to remember to stir every 10 minutes once my guest arrived. I didn't like this recipe very much.  But then again, I made some modifications to it by using dried rosemary and thyme. I would try the recipe again using fresh herbs, more olive oil and a 9x13 pan but I found it to be way too much work peeling and cutting up all those vegetables (specially the squash).

text:
Excellent dish!  I used sweet onions (instead of red-I don't like the texture of roasted red onions) and a yam (instead of a sweet potato, which gave more color and sweetness).  I cut all of my vegetables real big and chunky which made for a beautiful presentation, but did increase the cook time by about ten minutes. I cooked the root vegetables for 35 to 40 min. then put the peppers and onions in for the last 15 minutes of cook time, which another reviewer suggested. It really did make a difference and kept the peppers and onions bright and crisp. I made these for myself to eat over a few days, and they just got better as they sat in the fridge. Definitely give this one a try.
5 stars in my book.

text:
I served this at an annual Christmas Dinner for a ministerial association and it was a hit!  Since I was making it in a large quantity (every pan served 25 people), I decided to bake it @ 425 degrees to not get those black ends on the veggies when the temperature is too high.  It took 2 hours and the root veggies were still not perfectly done.  I ended up microwaving them for 5 minutes to soften the potatoes...it worked!  I must say that this is the best way to cook veggies for a crowd and still maintain your reputation as a great chef...there was not a potato or veggie left in the pans.  I did roast the root veggies for about an hour before I added the peppers, etc.  Thanks for a great recipe.

YUM! A wonderful hearty side for the winter! The recipe did make a LOT of veggies. I cut up all the vegetables and only roasted 1/2 first. I waved the rest and froze them. I roasted the rest of the veggies later. This worked out well. Freezing the potatoes and squash worked well and you simply have to add in fresh onion and red pepper out of the freezer. This way you don't have to worry about what you are going to use 1/2 a butternut squash for. Excellent flavor and good texture. NOTE: If you cook only 1/2 the vegetable, you only need to cook them for about 25-30 minutes.

text:
I gave the potatoes a decent cook in a skillet to ensure they cooked through in the oven while I chopped up the rest of the veggies.  I simply put everything onto a sheet pan lined with foil, drizzled the oil, vinegar and herbs on top, mixed well with clean hands and popped it into the oven. I kept an eye on it and gave it a stir about 20 minutes into the cooking time and just watched it from there, making sure it didn't burn. Used those little yellow & green zucchini/squash thingies, red onion, four smaller Yukon gold potatoes and one package of precut butternut squash. I didn't have fresh herbs and didn't feel like buying fresh so just used herbes de provence, salt and fresh ground black pepper. Easy and amazingly delicious ~ it was our main course. Will definitely be making again, with mushrooms added.

text:
Just me and hubby so I scaled this down to 4 servings.  Made as written, but eliminated the sweet potato & added zucchini, brussel sprouts cut in half, cauliflower bites, and whole mushrooms.  I took other reviewers suggestion & zapped the Yukon Gold potatoes in micro & cut into larger cubes.  Also as others suggested, lined baking sheet with parchment paper.  Baked at 450 degrees 15 minutes, stirred, added the mushrooms, then baked an additional 15 minutes.  The veggies were all roasted evenly browned and Delicious.  I made a BIG mistake and kept them warm in oven until my other dinner dish was ready.  The veggies 'dried' out, but still very tasty.  The following day I chopped the leftovers, and made a Spanish 'tortilla' for brunch.  A Spanish tortilla is made with potatoes, onions, and eggs, so this worked out well and just as tasty, but more nutritious.  Warning:  DO NOT allow to sit in a warm oven.  See photo which was taken prior to putting dish back in warm oven.  Enjoy ASAP, or re-warm later.  Will definitely be making this again.

text:
As a kick off to trying to eat better I thought I'd like to add more veggies to my diet. Never made roasted veggies. This was a great first attempt. I'm sure there's nothing to it but I'm glad I found this recipe. The smell was great even before going into the oven! I used a large butternut squash(never had before- only as creamed soup), tri-colored bell peppers, red potatoes, baby carrots and red onion. I would've used my sweet potato but was running out of room. I didn't have fresh rosemary and only dried thyme- so I just used 1 Tblsp italian seasoning(which contains morjoram, basil, thyme, oregano and rosemary). I will definitely make this again and again. Also I did use a little less than the called for 1/4 cup of oil. Per other reviews I used two pans, putting the squash  and potatoes on one and everything else on pan #2, I took pan #2 out after 30 mins and pan one out after 50ish. My daughters and I picked at this all day will actually make along side something next time-as this was a test run. Yum!!!

Haven't tried this yet but looks and sounds amazing. Just responding to previous comments complaints of the potatoes not being done while the veggies get overdone/mushy. I recently read a tip that sounds like it might work well for this situation. Before mixing all the veggies up, microwave your potatoes whole for just 2-3 minutes a piece in the microwave. This might help balance out the time differences and let the taters get crispy faster along with the veg.

text:
A little labor intensive, but worth all the chopping. The most difficult part was peeling the squash. I cut it into quarters, stood it on end and used my sharpest knife and cut straight down the outside to peel. I roast at 450, tenting if necessary. Just use common sense with the cooking times for the vegetables you are cooking. I think the submitter has a great combination as is, but I see where we all like to add our favorites. With dried spices, remember to use 1/3 the amount, for the amount of fresh. Next time I will use less potatoes & more sweet potatoes, (personal preference) I made again adding summer squash, mixing in at the very end. I love all vegetables but didn't care for zucchini in it. Even cooking for a very few minutes I found it to be too mushy for me.

text:
Awesome and works perfectly fine with dried herbs.  To the reviewer who gave it a bad review because s/he must have used WAY too much dried herbs: keep in mind that fresh herbs have water in them, making them larger and less strong.  Hence you always need MORE fresh herbs and LESS dried herbs.  A teaspoon or less (to taste) in this recipe would be fine.  That's what I did and it turned out delicious!

text:
First of all, I don't understand the person that rated the recipe a 2 when they didn't use fresh herbs the way the recipe states?  I am giving this recipe 4 stars only because I've made it half a dozen times now and it needs adjustments.  I have it nailed down now.  It's 5 stars if you do the following: Oven temp 450 instead of 475. Put potatoes, onion and carrots on one sheet to cook about 45 minutes.  Add the peppers, squash and zucchini to another pan and cook the last 20 minutes of the baking time.  Note, those are the veggies I typically use.  But, as long as you put the more delicate veggies in at the later time, it should be perfect.  I also add chopped fresh garlic to the oil mixture.

This was amazing!  Instead of Squash I used 2 sliced & chopped carrots. I left out mushrooms, we don't like them.  I substituted Apple Cider Vinegar for the balsamic.   I added about 1/2 teaspoon each of Oregano & Basil. I also used dried herbs for Thyme & Rosemary, thats what I have and it came out phenomenal!  I added 1 can of sweat Peas and 1 can of Soy Beans, both drained and 1 can petite diced tomatoes.  I took other reviewers suggestions and cooked the root veggies for about 20 minutes first at the 475degree.   Then I added the 3 cans of veggies with the bell pepper and mixed it all up.   Lowered the heat to 425 and added canned veggies to root veggie pan and cooked for additional 20 minutes.  This should still make about 12 servings.   With my substitutions the total Calories per serving are now: 210.  7 grams of fat per serving, 30 carbs per serving, 7 fiber grams per serving and 10 protein per serving.  So healthy and nutritious and best of all, so delicious!  This is super easy to cut, chop, prepare and bake.  What a joy!  This is a hit!  Thank you for posting this yummy dish!

text:
This is absolutely fabulous! Definitely a new favorite. 

**very important** If you can't find fresh herbs and have to use dried, you have to use 1/3 of the amount! So, the recipe calls for 2T fresh, you use 2t dried. 1T fresh=1t dried.  I suspect that's where the "overpowering" comments come from.

Cook the potatoes on one cookie sheet and the peppers, onions, and zucchini on another. The peppers etc. get done much faster (about 10 mins. They get overdone very easily). And cook the potatoes for about 20-30 mins. Spray the foil on the cookie sheets well. And stir veggies once or twice while cooking. Bake at 400 degrees. text:
After reading the reviews and looking at my Indian slow cooker cook book - I made the following changes: I used 2 eggplant, 1 large potato, a chopped onion, 3 fresh tomatoes, and I made rather large matchsticks out of a big carrot.(I skipped the winter squash and bell pepper) I then took 1 Tablespoon of Garam Marasala, 1 Tablespoon of Cumin not seeds and a Tablespoon of sea salt with 6 Tablespoons of olive oil and heated it up over the stove top letting the heat bring out the favors. I then took the spice mix and poured it over the big bowl of prepared veggies and tossed well. When all the veggies are covered I covered the large bowl with plastic wrap and let it sit in the fridge over night. The next day I dumped the whole thing in the crock pot for about 4 hours on high and added 2 cinnamon sticks.Do not add water! Because the crock pot cooks veggies differently it will not be mushy after 4 hours. Remove the cinnamon sticks and WOW! Out of this world good and spicey so your lips felt it but not too hot. Great basic recipe! Thanks for the ideas.

text:
Wonderful recipe, and very versatile!  This is a great way to roast lots of different veggies.  Fresh rosemary, fresh thyme, and red peppers are a must.  I've made this many times.   I've used different kinds of winter squash, different kinds of potatoes (gold, red, white but not russet), added fennel bulb (delicious richness when roasted), added carrots (wonderful sweetness), added cherry tomatoes, subbed white for red onions, thrown a bit of garlic powder into the marinade.  Just a hint: remember that potatoes/squash will take the longest to cook per size; make sure they are all about the same size and larger chunks of onion and/or bell pepper are ok.  DELICIOUS!!!

Wonderful. I agree with some of the reviewers, toss in the onions, peppers a little later to keep their colour. I chose different vegetables, including celery, carrots, sweat peas and Jerusalem artichokes (so yummy!). Will redo this on a very regular basis--great to get the whole family to have a large portion of vegetables.

text:
It's hard to review "roasted vegetables" because roasting vegetables is always a favorite.  You can do anything you want with what you do and do not put in the recipe, and, assuming you're a veggie lover, it's going to be good. I personally made several changes to this recipe: omitted squash, added brocolli, substitued oregano and garlic powder for the listed spices.  I also sauteed onions/mushrooms in butter and garlic towards the end of the roasting, and pour that over the finished product. Regardless of whether you make these changes or not, this is a hearty vegetable dish that should be remembered for hearty dinners and parties. The only word of caution: cut the potatoes no bigger than 1/4 inch thick, and sized no bigger than a quarter so that they won't take forever to cook.

text:
I've taken the basic gist of this recipe and other Roasted Veggie recipes on this site and made them according to my own specifications on several occasions. The basic premise of roasting vegetables is very simple which makes this recipe the ideal combination of -'flexible' & 'easy'.

There's no butternut squash in this part of the world and I'm not sure what Yukon Gold potatoes are...so my medley of veggies rotates between a combination of the following: regular potatoes (thinly sliced), sliced beetroot (semi-cooked in a pressure cooker beforehand, one whistle), carrots and baby corn sliced long, red & yellow bell peppers, cherry tomatoes, sliced mushrooms, zucchini, onions, green beans, broccoli, eggplant......really whatever you have in the veggie crisper works. 
All of this is drizzled with olive oil and for seasoning: crushed garlic (7-8 cloves sometimes!), a dash of organic rock salt, ground pepper, red chili flakes, fresh basil/thyme/oregano, a bay leaf, a squeeze of lemon or very little balsamic vinegar. 
Let the veggies sit for a while before roasting, makes it more flavorful-- I cook between 180 to 200 C (400F) on the convection setting on my microwave for about 15 minutes. Some people keep the root veggies for longer and then add the squishier veggies like tomatoes and eggplant in during the last 10 to 15 mins but I put everything in at once because I'm lazy. Overall, quite a winner and the slacker's way out of cooking dinner (esp. if you can get someone to do the

text:
Delicious!!!  I have long been a fan of roasting carrots or potatoes in the oven with just olive oil, salt, and pepper, but this combination of veggies with the vinaigrette is great.  I used baby carrots instead of squash (wanted to try squash but it looked bad at the market), and I made a large amount of the dressing, put in some minced garlic, and put the dressing with all the prepared veggies in a large resealable bag.  I let them marinate in the fridge for a couple of hours, but I think even longer would have been better.  I spread them out on a rimmed baking sheet, and cooked them for probably 40 minutes, stirring every 10 minutes as the recipe states.
We had this as a side dish to pork tenderloin, and I think it would be a fantastic side to ANY meat.  Also would be great for entertaining since you end up with a TON of veggies!
HIGHLY HIGHLY HIGHLY recommend!

text:
This dish is wonderful to have as a delicious healthy snack for lunch time, or to serve the family as a side dish with dinner. I used two gallon size zip lock bags to shake the fresh cut veggies in a low fat balsamic vinaigrette, lemon pepper, dried oregano, and a little extra olive oil. I added a few sliced carrots, two jalepenos, and a few cups of broccoli florets. Shaking the veggies in the sauce with those seasonings, and letting them soak for 30 minutes in that before baking,  turned out perfectly. The broccoli and carrots were an excellent addition if you have those on hand. My oven cooked this dish best at 425F, stirring every 10 minutes, taking about 50 minutes to caramelize the onions and sweet potatoes. Hope this information helps! Thank you for the recipe!

I have done vegetables this way for years, although without balsamic vinegar.  I do add garlic. This is the first thing I've cooked since chicken and frozen vegetables in about 15 years (no exaggeration). I had a craving for roasted veggies, found this recipe on my phone in the produce aisle. I had to watch videos to figure out how to cut the squash and herbs. (Yes, that's how little I know about cooking.) I never salt my food and didn't include it in the recipe. Really easy and ingredients can easily be added or deleted to your liking.  I make this all the time with whatever veggies I have on hand.  I also change up the herbs and flavored vinegar!  This recipe is easy to manipulate to your taste, so give it a try.  One thing I have learned is that I prefer to cook my root vegetables for about 20 minutes before adding all my other vegetables.  This allows for the same texture throughout and I don't end up with super soft ingredients.  I never have left overs!

EASY! I was surprised at how good this was! This is something I'll be making over and over again. The only thing I noticed was the vegetables didn't "brown" like I expected. I made ~3/4 of the full recipe and should have probably taken it out around 35-40min. I left it in for over 45min and the veggies got a little mushy, but it was still delicious. I was worried b/c I used a butternut squash that wasn't quite ripe yet, but it came out just fine. I also used dried thyme and rosemary, but only a pinch of thyme. Make sure you carefully read the conversion from fresh to dried on their containers. Highly recommend this dish!

text:
This recipe is incredibly delicious!  It's easily adaptable to whatever vegetables you have on hand.   This last time, I didn't have fresh thyme, so I used one teaspoon dried thyme, and it was still wonderful.   I've made it in the oven, on the barbecue, and even once over an open fire, as a foil-wrapped bundle.  ***Update:  I've started making this regularly, and varying the veggies according to what I have on  hand.  I've used various squash, parsnips, and carrots in addition to what's in the recipe.  HEALTHY AND TIME-SAVING TIP:   stop peeling those veggies!  The healthiest part of the veggie is in the outer layer.  Just use a vegetable brush to clean the veggies before you chop them.  (If you're concerned about pesticide residues, and you should be, buy organic.)  I've used pumpkin instead of butternut squash, and even pumpkin skin becomes tender once it's roasted.  Thanks or posting, Saundra!

text:
Love roasted vegetables!
For added color I used one yellow and one red bell pepper; added cauliflower in place of butternut squash, and added garlic cloves (cut in big chunks) 'love the garlic'. 
I used balsamic glaze, preferring a stronger flavor. Best to drizzle the glaze directly on the vegetables, then add the oil-spice mixture and toss to coat.
I used 1 teaspoon dried thyme, didn't have fresh (remember to adjust measurement between dried and fresh). I did have fresh rosemary from my garden, but only used 1 tablespoon. I find these herbs to be a bit bitter.
I used baby gold potato's cut in half. I like the look of little potato compared to cubes. I microwaved the gold and sweet potato's, and cauliflower till slightly cooked. It helps everything cook evenly with other ingredients when in the oven. NO hard potato's please. I also wanted brussel sprouts, which I cut in quarters and microwaved them slightly, but DANG! if I didn't get distracted and forgot them in the microwave. I confess, I found them next morning. Yuk.
I reduced the temp to 450 for 50 minutes. This is a colorful dish, although the vegi's brown out when reheated next day.
 I made this dish for a special church potluck, they ate it all.  I found out later, one of our dinner guests loved it so much, he sneaked a bowlful to take home. He couldn't stop raving about this delicious dish.
My next batch will include mushrooms and, of course, brussel sprouts; and maybe basil as mentioned in another review. Mini roma t

text:
Delicious.  A bit time-consuming to prep all of the vegetables, but well worth it.  Ingredient changes: I used 1 tsp. dried thyme, 2 tsp. dried rosemary, 1/8 c. oil, 3 T. balsamic vinegar, 1 tsp. garlic powder,  1 tsp. basil 2 red onions and 2 bunches of broccoli.  Recipe changes: I mixed the herbs first to blend the flavors, and preheated the oven to 450. I used 2 baking sheets with parchment paper cut to size, lightly sprayed with Pam.  I put the onions, potatoes, and squash (root veggies) in first, covered with foil.  After 10-15 minutes, I added the peppers and broccoli and covered with foil.  Cook with foil covering for first half, then remove for 2nd half so veggies brown up nicely.  Make sure to stir every 10 minutes or so, and total cooking time is 30-40 minutes.  I will try baby carrots, zucchini, new potatoes, grape tomatoes and mushrooms in the future. I added these to my lunch for a week and they were so good!

text:
BEST ROASTED VEGETABLES I HAVE EVER MADE!!  I used whatever veggies I had in the fridge, which happen to be baby carrots, green bell pepper, broccoli, onion, and russet potatoes.  I took the advice of others and put the carrots and potatoes in the oven to cook for 30 minutes, then added bell pepper, onion, and broccoli and cooked for an additional 10 minutes.  Everything was cooked perfectly. I mixed the oil, balsamic, dried thyme, dried rosemary, salt, and pepper in a bowl then poured the mixture over all of the veggies, lightly coating them.  Several people have said not to use dried herbs in this recipe.  I used them and thought it turned out great although fresh herbs are preferred.  The key is to keep in mind that the measurements for dried herbs vs fresh is different.  1 tbsp fresh does not equal 1 tbsp of dried.  A small amount of dried goes a long way, use very sparingly.  I used just a pinch of the thyme and rosemary and added salt and pepper.  I will definitely be cooking my veggies this way for now on.

Ignore the most critical reviews - obviously these people can't read. This recipe clearly calls for fresh rosemary and thyme and the people who left low stars are the only ones who deserve them for thinking dried herbs in a recipe that calls for baking will work as well as fresh. Dried herbs don't emit the same fragrances and oils as fresh herbs do in the oven because they have already been in the oven. It's sense! 

This recipe is delicious and great to make in bulk. I section mine off into portions and freeze them, then throw them in with the rest of my meal prep for the week.

I mixed red potatoes and real carrots (sliced to be about baby carrot size) onions and a few cloves of garlic with the onions mixed in one bowl with enough oil/balsamic mixture to coat. I used fresh thyme and 1 tbsp of Italian seasonings since there was no fresh rosemary available at the market. In a second bowl I combined zucchini and yellow bell peppers and finish tossing with the rest of the oil/balsamic mixture. I put the potatoes and carrot bowl in a glass pan with a little bit of  plain oil in the bottom of the pan and cooked for about 40 mins. I planned to add the zucchini and bell peppers in the same pan but I was afraid they would finish cooking at separate time so I added them to another pan and cooked for about 20 mins. Then I added all the vegetables together once they were out of the over. I'm no cooking expert but It came out tender and delicious and released the natural flavor of the vegetables!

text:
This was so delicious!  My husband and I loved it. As other reviewers, I just used the vegetables that I had: potatoes, carrots, zucchini, celery, onions, sweet mini peppers,and garlic.  I only added salt, pepper, and dry Italian seasoning only because it was what I had that was close to the original recipe. I roasted the potatoes and carrots at 375 degrees for about 20-25 min before including the other vegetables (to prevent burning of the more fragile veggies as suggested), being sure to stir well so that the olive oil and balsamic vinegar coated them well. I added additional salt and pepper as well. The total cooking time was about 40-45 min. Very pleased with the result and will definitely make this again.

So delicious!! Even my fiance, the avid carnivore, dove in for seconds! I didn't change out any of the ingredients and I made sure the veggies were cut small like another poster said to avoid uncooked veggies while others got mushy. I also did the cook 1/2 the time with foil cover and 1/2 without to avoid mushy veggies. My fiance mixed this recipe with "Flat Iron Steak with Balsamic Reduction" and  they played together beautifully (although the 1st time around, I burned the sauce and didn't include it). As a leftover, I mixed with a Vegan version of "Brown Sugar Meatloaf" and it was gorgeous! Great recipe!!

Our favored veggies were the red peppers, then the onions.  We had a couple problems with this recipe.  The Yukon gold potatoes were very dry and not tasty; some of the sweet potatoes were overdone and mushy.  I swapped carrots for the squash (only I barely like squash) and they were cooked perfectly.  I also added a few leftover mushrooms for the last 10 minutes and they were excellent.  I will say that as I've been reheating the veggies, I really believe the flavors of this recipe are a '5'.  The Yukon Golds tho still don't seem to have a lot of flavor.  I had huge Yukons, so maybe that was part of the problem.

This was really good, but mine was nowhere near done after 40 minutes!  Maybe my roasting pan was not big enough, as I used a deep pan and it was fairly full.  After the first 40 minutes I added foil and left them in for another 20 minutes without stirring, then took the foil off and left them in another 10 minutes.  The vegetables had good flavor but I think I will need some time to perfect this recipe.  Only change was that I used garlic infused olive oil for extra flavor.  I've also made this with sweet potatoes, yams, parnips, zucchini, brussels sprouts, shallots, and whole cloves of garlic - yum!

Again, I have to echo other reviewers' sentiments stating that you must use FRESH rosemary and thyme for best results. Also, I found the the variety of veg listed in this recipe to be a bit high -- so I used only half the amount of potatoes (I used small red potatoes cut in halves, smaller than other veg pieces since potatoes cook slower than other veg), mushroom, red onion, zucchini, yellow squash, butternut squash, baby carrots. This turned out to be a favorite among my friends when I served at a dinner party. I think the balsamic vinegar really brings the flavor together. Highly recommend!

text:
I used this recipe as a template (used potatoes, sweet potatoes, onions, carrots, and garlic cloves, yum!), since roasting veggies is a really flexible affair. I loved the addition of the balsamic vinegar - subtle but worth it! The one thing I will say is that this will NOT be ready after 40 min in the oven. I cut my potatoes very small, about 3/4- to 1/2-in. cubes, and they still take more than an hour to be cooked through and not crunchy. Just plan accordingly, though, and you'll enjoy the results of this recipe! Having this is like Thanksgiving whenever I want :) Thanks!

Great recipe!  Although it takes some time to peel and cut up all the veggies, it's worth it.  Perfect combination of sweet and salty.  I used Sierra Gold potatoes b/c I couldn't find Yukon Golds and it worked out just fine.  Cooked for 40 minutes at 475 and it was perfect.  Potatoes had a nice texture, not too hard.  Be sure to stir every 10 minutes or onions will turn brown and crisp.  And fresh herbs really do make a difference!

text:
Excellent recipe!  I found that it works better if you cook the vegetables in different batches.  First, start with onions, bell peppers (I used red, orange, yellow peppers.  Looked really pretty), potatoes, and sweet potatoes.  After about 25 minutes, I added zucchini and asparagas.  This way, the latter vegetables don't get overcooked.  You can add other vegetables too, just make sure you time them so that they all get cooked perfectly.  The sweet potatoes are great in this recipe!

I made the exact recipe except I substituted dried thyme and rosemary for fresh (using the same amounts indicated). It turned out delicious! My only warning is that the prep time took almost an hour. I could probably have saved 15 minutes if I bought pre-cut squash, as that took up a good chunk of the time.

This would be a fantastic side dish on Thanksgiving. Next time I think I will add one yellow bell pepper and one orange bell pepper for some beautiful color. I cooked at 475 degrees for 35 minutes and that seemed to be just the right amount of time. I did stir and flip the vegetables halfway through. The family really enjoyed this one!

text:
A classic recipe for winter vegetables.  I always use just enough oil to lightly coat the vegetables; this is actually less than one tablespoon, added by itself.  I check the vegetables for softness throughout the cooking time and if one vegetable is lagging behind I quickly cut them in half.  Also, at 475 the onions tend to burn so I add them a little bit later in the cooking process.  Fresh rosemary is a must for this recipe, and adding a whole bulb of peeled garlic is also nice.

I made this for me and my wife. I had to make a couple changes, but mostly stuck with the recipe. I put a tiny amount of rosemary, as my wife doesn't care for a very strong rosemary. I also completely left out the ginger, as my wife will not eat ginger, saying even in small amounts, that she doesn't like it. I believe the prep time to be off. I know I'm not the fastest chef around, but would love to meet the person who can peel and cut the Vegetables in less than 1 hours. But with those things said, we absolutely loved it! The recipe is definitely for a large party, and we ate it for 3 meals. That is no worry though as I believe it's even better reheated! I believe I will fix it for Thanksgiving!

Excellent, but I made some changes:  I used convection oven at 400.  Ingredients were Brussels sprouts, pepper, 1 corn cut into 4ths; green beans, mushroom, 1 red potato, and 1 red onion.  Once cut up I added all in bag with olive oil; then dumped into a 9x13 glass pan.  To that I Added herb du province, salt, pepper, oregano, rosemary; then balsamic.  Cooked for 30 min, then covered with foil for another 20.  Added a handful of chapped parsley and turned the oven off and left it while making salmon with teriyaki on the stove for about 15 minutes.  Came out awesome!

The flavour was nice, but I found that certain veggies are done before others , therefore some things were mushy.  I made it a second time but this time I separated the veggies,  I used two cookie sheets and spread them out. e.g. potatoes and squash together because they took about the same time.  I used carrots and beets. beets took the longest time.  Pepper's the least.  That way I could keep an eye on them and remove them separately as they were done.

This was a big hit.  I did as some others suggested and cooked the root veggies separately.  I put those in the oven for 20 minutes at 475.  Then I brought the temp down to 425.  I have a double oven, so I put the other veggies in the other oven at 475 and cooked them all for another 20 minutes.

text:
I loved this! I did make some changes/additions that worked perfectly. In total all the veggies I used was the butternut squash, red onion, sweet potatoes, golden potatoes, red bell pepper, and zucchini. I own the KitchenAid food processor attachment and I used it to dice every vegetable to the same size. I feel like using fresh thyme and rosemary was also very necessary. This worked perfect in the oven at 450 for 25-30 minutes. Nothing was overdone and nothing was underdone. Will definitely make it like this again. I liked having everything the same small size because you could get all the veggies in with one bite.

text:
Yummy and super-easy, a hit at all the holiday parties. I thought a whole red onion would be too much, but by the end of the roasting process it's just right. Give yourself a few minutes extra in case the squash and yams (which I used instead of sweet potatoes) aren't quite done at 40 minutes. I added chunks of Granny Smith apple. They are pretty well stewed by 40 minutes but add a nice bit of sweet. If you want them firmer, throw them in half-way through.

text:
Despite what another reviewer said, I made this using dried thyme and rosemary instead of fresh and it turned out really well! The rule of thumb is to use 1/3 the amount when you are substituting because dried herbs are stronger than fresh. I didn't have any red peppers so I used carrots instead and I didn't have a red onion so I used a yellow onion instead. Also, my sweet potato was huge so I used the whole thing and omitted the yukon gold potatoes. I roasted everything together for the same amount of time on two cookie sheets--one on the top rack and one on the bottom but both near the middle of the oven. I stirred only once. YUM.

text:
Delicious! I tweaked the recipe according to the recommendations I read. Instead of using butternut squash, I substituted zucchini and carrots. And I roasted the onion, carrots, yam and potatoes first for 30 minutes then added the zucchini+pepper second, roasting for an additional 10-15 minutes. Very important to use a nonstick roasting pan - I made the vegetables a second time using a glass Pyrex dish and it was messy/sticky and it didn't come out as well. Great recipe!

text:
We enjoyed the flavors of this recipe, although I do think that the potatoes, sweet potato and squash were all a bit..repetitive. Dominant flavor was definitely the rosemary; the squash and the sweet potato also added a lot of sweetness. This tasted much better right out of the oven; I would eat it the next day but wouldn't serve it to company on the second day.

 I definitely used more than 2 tablespoons of balsamic vinegar- maybe closer to three. We probably didn't need to chop the veggies up as much as we did. It too forever to prepare everything! Used aluminum foil, which worked well but should've sprayed the foil as some of the veggies ended up sticking to the sheet and there was some burning. I also forgot to stir the veggies...

text:
--Since I personally do not like too much white potato in the recipe, I  decided to eliminate the Yukon potatoes, and instead, added two fresh cubed beets and one yam. I also used 2 red onion and 3 red bell pepper. The extra red pepper, red onion, beets, and yam to this recipe caramelize well during the roasting process adding extra yummy sweetness! Also, since I didn't have access to fresh herbs, I used 2 Tblsp of dried Italian seasoning instead.

I did not use any potatoes or other squash as my intention for this recipe is to put the veggies on a sandwich bun with a few slices of brie and lettuce tomorrow for lunch. I tossed the veggies every 10 min for 35-37 minutes.

text:
This was pretty good. I've made it twice now. I didn't feel the butternut squash made any difference in flavor. Second time I made it with chopped yellow squash instead and made a huge difference. The red peppers don't do much for it (taste-wise) as well. I still add them because they are healthy but if you want to save money, don't bother. The potatoes take longer to cook than everything else so I cook it for 10 min longer than suggested (50 min) and toss the veggies while cooking every 6-8 minute because the onions burn easily. All in all its a good veggie side and will make it again.

text:
Super easy.  One of those recipes that you can do slight changes to each week and it never gets boring. (Changes such as different veggies, with or without potatoes, balsamic vinegar or lemon juice, sprinkle feta cheese or parmesan cheese, or no cheese on top before serving, etc.). Remember to adjust cooking time accordingly.  This recipe is for 12 servings - more like 24!  I cut it to 2 servings and had plenty.  For those who complain about the amount of chopping: I used pre-cut veggies from store.  And, as I chopped up mushrooms, red pepper, etc I kept small amounts aside and used them for our dinner salads.  Thanks!

text:
I made this as a main dish for one, intending to save half, use stock to deglaze the pan and make soup with the other half... but it's gone. Whoops!
I had to make a couple of substitutions. I didn't have any balsamic vinegar(gasp!), so I used two good splashes of homemade herbal vinegar. I didn't have fresh thyme, so I used fresh oregano. I also used an unknown type of squash (Long and oblong with a very hard woody shell; orange flesh and brown seeds - any guesses?)for the first time, and it was unbelievably good roasted! The trick is to leave them roast until just before the point of burning, so they get a lovely carmelized taste. I cooked mine in a rice cooker, because I don't have an oven.

This was super easy and fabulous. Will definitely make again.

Perfection!  This was everything I expected it to be.  I used sweet potatoes, red potatoes, onion, mushrooms, and green peppers and used a combination of dried and fresh herbs.  Don't be afraid to liberally sprinkle more seasonings to your taste; I found I had to add more s & p and a touch of garlic powder.  Oh, and I also added a splash of lemon juice.  I opted to turn the heat down to around 430 and roast the potatoes  and onion first, then after about 35 minutes, I added the mushrooms and peppers.  Very very good! Thank you for posting this recipe!
